ClassicFrank</user_name>
<time>1510776016311<//time><Rate>4<//Rate>< text>
Wonderful place to shop for clothes, furniture, and other items when on a tight budget!

While the inside is a tad run down it's kept up pretty well and there is always a good selection of items. It also has a wheelchair accessible ramp up to the store which is great for anyone who might otherwise be unable to go there.

The items there include clothes for under $10, sometimes even new. They also have excellent furniture as well as washers and dryers which were great if on a very tight budget.  It is good to note not everything is cheaper at thrift stores as sometimes new can be the same price, however this is usually not the case.

On Thursday I believe there is 50% off of all items and I'm not sure about other days, but it tends to become very crowded during the half off day. There is a senior discount, though I can't recall what it is.

Overall it's a great place for clothes, furniture, kitchen items, and even has some great electronics if you know what your looking for.< /text>

< review>
This very special little restaurant is a treasure. The site design is beautiful. The rear window shows a lush garden. The dining room is well designed taking into consideration comfort and noise management. All of this pales when compared with the food, wine and service.
The menu is small, but it covers the bases. Food is fresh and seasonal. I'm not sure my words can do justice to the food. It's magnificent. We enjoyed succulent little oysters, portobello fritters, lasagne and salmon. For dessert we had the sticky toffee pudding. I would encourage people to go experience this little haven. Be prepared you pay for the quality.</review>

The service here was terrific, which is really nice to have when you are out for a special occasion. Unfortunately the food did not deliver. The "saffron paella" did not seem to contain any saffron and did not much resemble paella. It did contain some lovely fresh peas. The duck dish was far too sweet and floral, so difficult to enjoy. The salad was overdressed and dull at the same time; the portabella fritters were good. The deviled eggs tasted mostly of Dijon mustard. My husband thinks they were trying to be too "experimental". That being said, if you are not too concerned with the cuisine, the place is lovely and the people who work there are wonderful. They will do their best to make sure you have a nice dining experience.<//Text>

<user_name>Emily Luthra<//user_name>< Text>
Best restaurant in the bay area. Consistently superb food, drinks, and desserts. They do the most amazing things with chickpeas. I often order their vegetarian dishes because they do better vegetarian than anywhere else. Worth the long drive, if you're on the other side of the bay area. And affordable -- much pricier bay area restaurants never come close to Rivoli's quality of execution.< /Text>

< Review>
I have never had a bad meal at Rivoli.  Come to think of it, I have never had a meal that wasn't great.  The food is excellent and the dining room, though a bit small and sometimes cramped, has a wonderfully romantic feel.  One of my favorite things about Rivoli is the wine list.  Nearly every bottle is under $100 and most are under $50.  The somelier doesn't try to overwhelm you with a long wine list, but rather has chosen ~4 pages of full bottles and 1 page of half bottles that all pair wonderfully with the food.< /Review>

<time>1477862660619</time><Rating>2< /Rating><Review>My wife took me here for my birthday after painstakingly searchung for good restaurant in the Berkeley area. I thanked my wife for taking me here on my birthday and amazingly the maitre 'd must have heard me because he treated us to a sundae with celebratory candles which I thought was a nice gesture.

However, the service was sub par. I could see the place was busy but I also saw 3 waiters serving a room of about 25-30 people. Our server kept bumping into me as he was serving the table next to us and several times I had to lean out of the way so he wouldn't hit me as he was serving, clearing, and pouring water. I didn't care for him reaching across my face to pour. We spent almost 200 dollars for the dinner and my wife ate half her meal, requesting a box to take home. They completely forgot her leftovers after she specifically asked for TWO separate boxes. This was no cheap meal and she didn't get to finish it.

I will state for the record that I value my wife's taste and was definitely exited to try a new eatery based on her opinion. We both agree that we felt the service started out well but then deteriorated into feeing like we were being neglected and forgotten. If they wanted to clear the table for waiting patrons, they should have been more attentive. They expect a high premium for there food. We deserved an equal caliber of service.

< Text>
Veggie Today is new to our area, and a very welcome addition. Their menu is extensive, they are open for lunch and dinner, and they will work with you for special dietary needs. We had green beans and tofu over rice, a sesame and eggplant dish and curry vegetables over rice. All were excellent. The service was pleasant and fast. We look forward to going back here again and again to eat their healthy dishes. The restaurant is small, but pleasantly decorated. It is just two blocks from Todos Santos Plaza, west of Concord Ave. on Salvio St. There is lots of free parking around. It is about a 15 minute walk from the Concord BART Station.</Text>

<text>This place is really amazing. I was with three other people and we all ordered different items to share. The food is 100% veggitaren and made to represent the real thing. The food itself is an interesting variety of different Chinese dishes and the cooks seem to care about how they prepare your food. Everything is very well priced and you get alot for your money! Three main dishes a large salad and two appetizers came up to around $54.

The building looks like a standard Chinese hole in the wall restaurant. There is a television that plays the usually sports or news. The dishes and utensils are of the same standard.

I am not a vegetarian (I eat meat about three times a week) because I haven't found something that could replace meat. Veggie Today is definitely a place to go if you are looking for a vegetarian meal that taste like the real thing!

I'd recommend the dish 5.1. I really enjoyed it and if I didn't know that it wasn't meat I wouldn't have figured it out.< /text>< user_name>

< review>
GERMANY üá©üá™
Eat the World LA review:
Anytime you are not in Germany, currywurst is a dish that there just is not enough around for satisfaction. Some renditions are around town but fall flat, even in good environments. Here at Grand Central Market, the environment is not terrific, but the dish is done right. Berlin Currywurst is originally from Los Angeles, but has also set up another shop in New York City. It offers a fairly compact list of options, something of a necessity for this market.
¬∞
Dive straight in and make one with the original style bratwurst and original curry sauce, served with bread. The menu lets you dictate your sausage and your sauce, so follow your original with the k√§se (filled with cheese) on your second visit. Curry spice levels can be adjusted as well, and 3 out of 4 was already giving great kick.
¬∞
Add a side of fries, knowing that one of life's simple pleasures is dipping one in both good curry sauce and mayonnaise, which is available in a squeeze bottle. Most importantly, the little stand has a beer and wine license, and a few selections of German beer. Sausage and beer is not rocket science, but it kind of is at the same time.<//review>

<Gmap_id>0x80c2c64b8e8c7a6b:0x1c031ecdfc1d81ff<//Gmap_id><UserId.>103234384634062553837< /UserId.><Date>1457744001923<//Date><rate>4<//rate><Name>Rosanna Chan<//Name><Pics>None< /Pics></record>

<Date>1430462316832<//Date>< Rating>
3< /Rating>
<text>A native Berliner reviewing a Currywurst stand in LA - and trust me, I'd love to give this little business some more credit as the idea of bringing original Berlin Currywurst to LA deserves 5 stars, let alone the use of the Berlin bear, the logo of the city.

Currywurst originated from Berlin, invented by Herta Heuwer in the late 1940's. It's basically a slightly fried pork sausage, topped with a special ketchup (the secret sauce!) and curry flavor. Sounds simple, but it's soooo good.

At the Berlin Currywurst stand in the Grand Central Market you'll get a decent tasting Currywurst either on a paper plate (original) or in a bun (American). You can add fries (original) or Sauerkraut (American).

But folks, $6 for one small Currywurst?! You gotta be kidding me. This is street food. It's like selling a taco for $5 just because it's from Mexico. Also, $4 for a super small side of Sauerkraut is nothing but ridiculous.

After paying $11 for a tiny Currywurst and a spoon of Sauerkraut my stomach felt as empty as before and I queued up at the Thai stand to get a plate of fried rice. Wow. I just paid $20 for my lunch.</text>< Pics>
None< /Pics>

<time>1549735209263< /time><Review>My favorite Chinese buffet in the entire LAX area. I could choose anywhere in LA to stay as I travel for work, but I choose Inglewood anywhere near the new Rams stadium they're building because it's right next to LAX so I can get to the airport in a few minutes and the traffic is way better to access the different interstates and highways. Not to mention the city seems to be nicer than the descriptions I've heard years ago since I'm from Georgia.
The Chinese restaurant is within walking distance from my hotel and they charge by the pound so I can determine how little a quantity I want instead of having to choose an item based off of it's set price. This place  has a mix between Chinese, Korean and Mongolian style dishes. My favorite choices there are the pork galbi (Korean style short ribs), the peppered chicken and the coconut shrimp is to die for! The best coconut shrimp  I ever had in my life. They have lomain, fried rice and also give the choice of regular white rice! Yeeeeeessss! I'm half Korean and white rice is what I crave when I have a choice. You can also stand in line and get the traditional Mongolian style food cooked in front of you as well. I think the price is between $3 or $4 per pound. I got 3 to go boxes for $17 last time I went which was less than $6 per person. I haven't been eating Chinese much these days until I came across this place now I eat it as regular as I do all the other restaurants and comes out to be cheaper than McDonald's or burger king</Review>< user_id>
